  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{83.016}{275.540}{50.738}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{9.796}{Winkelman.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{133.739}{275.540}{55.904}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{9.796}{ALIUS Bulletin}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{83.016}{287.099}{170.000}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{9.796}{\href{https://doi.org/10.34700/krg3-zk35}{https://doi.org/10.34700/krg3-zk35}}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{320.632}{45.118}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.547}{Abstract}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{340.403}{442.772}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{In this interview, Michael Winkelman and Martin Fortier discuss the extent to which}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{354.397}{442.778}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{consciousness is grounded in deep evolutionary mechanisms and can be enculturated.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{368.391}{442.779}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{First, the main tenets of two neuroanthropological approaches to consciousness and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{382.385}{442.773}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{culture are outlined. Next, the upsides and downsides of evolutionary psychology are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{396.379}{442.776}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{examined; the fruitfulness of this approach in the study of cultural phenomena such as}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{410.373}{442.777}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{shamanism is debated. The authors then discuss the promises of the "big data" approach to}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{424.367}{442.774}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{the study of religion as well as evolutionary puzzles about religion. Turning to issues}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{438.361}{442.778}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{bearing on the taxonomy of consciousness, the interview explores how consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{452.355}{442.775}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{should be individuated and especially how many "modes" of consciousness should be}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{466.350}{442.772}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{identified based on what we know of the biology and phenomenology of altered}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{480.344}{442.780}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{consciousness. Winkelman's concepts of the "integrative mode of consciousness" and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{494.338}{442.777}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{"psychointegrators" are subsequently examined. Next, the interview addresses both how}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{508.332}{442.773}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{alterations of consciousness are universally similar (the perennialist view) and can also be}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{522.326}{442.784}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{enculturated (the constructivist view). Finally, the authors discuss issues around the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{536.320}{442.781}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{cultural use of hallucinogens (a.k.a. visionary plants): what is the best method to study}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{550.314}{243.830}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{11.662}{them? And for how long have humans used them?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{119.909}{581.788}{400.350}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{10.729}{altered states of consciousness, enculturation, evolutionary neuroanthropology, hallucinogens,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{581.834}{42.252}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{10.623}{keywords:}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{594.616}{52.900}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{10.729}{shamanism.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{624.955}{442.833}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Your work is very multidisciplinary and spans several fields (at least the following:}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{639.649}{442.811}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{cultural anthropology, neuroanthropology, neurotheology, cognitive science of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{654.109}{442.756}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{religion, evolutionary anthropology, medical anthropology and evolutionary}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{668.803}{442.830}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{psychology). What was your training like? Who were the most important inspirational}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{683.497}{210.196}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{figures in your intellectual development?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{709.556}{440.496}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{I wandered from psychology to anthropology to cross-cultural psychology and cross-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{726.116}{443.626}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{cultural studies (ethnology, holocultural studies) to Buddhist psychology, then the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{742.443}{443.849}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{neurosciences and neurophenomenology and evolutionary psychology in the search}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

\noindent\begin{tikzpicture}[remember picture,overlay,x=1bp,y=1bp,shift={(current page.north west)}]
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-65.268bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.233bp);
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-777.332bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.466bp);
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{46}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.223}{443.712}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{of a method for understanding the biological bases of spiritual phenomena. My}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{97.550}{443.607}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{training was eclectic, largely self-driven; I went to graduate school at the School of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{114.109}{443.756}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Social Sciences, University of California, but most of my coursework was}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{130.669}{443.605}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{independent study. I was in search of the next paradigm, so the current paradigms}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{146.995}{443.725}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{seemed little relevant. But there were some important figures along the way.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{163.555}{440.496}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Intellectually, I was inspired by the work of Charles Laughlin, especially his co-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{180.115}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{authored Brain, Symbol and Experience (Laughlin, McManus, \& D'Aquili, 1990)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{196.441}{443.684}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{which set the foundation for the neurophenomenological approaches.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{213.001}{447.934}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Unfortunately, I did not grasp the full significance of Laughlin's co-authored The}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{76.333}{229.560}{444.997}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Spectrum of Ritual (D'Aquili, Laughlin, \& McManus, 1979) when I first read it, but}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{246.120}{216.126}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{this too eventually influenced my work.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{274.171}{442.866}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Most of your research work tackles topics in neuroanthropology. Importantly, the field}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{288.631}{442.820}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{of neuroanthropology is split, as it were, between two distinct schools. The first}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{303.325}{96.936}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{coincides with the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{175.618}{303.325}{111.384}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{biogenetic structuralist}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{286.977}{303.325}{233.531}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{approach as defined by the seminal work of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{317.785}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Charles Laughlin and colleagues (Laughlin \& D'Aquili, 1974; Laughlin et al., 1990).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{332.479}{442.630}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{According to this school, the brain is endowed with many innate and universal neural}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{346.940}{442.813}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(or "neurognostic") structures that explain behaviors and beliefs observed across the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{361.633}{442.857}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{world. The second school is more recent and is best epitomized by the volume edited}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{376.094}{214.366}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{by Daniel Lende \& Greg Downey (2012),}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{292.674}{376.094}{101.144}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{The encultured brain}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{393.843}{376.094}{126.655}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{, and by work in cultural}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{390.788}{442.898}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{neuroscience conducted by Joan Chiao and colleagues (2016). The work of Andreas}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{405.248}{442.888}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Roepstorff and coworkers (2010) also belongs to this approach. In contrast to the first}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{419.942}{442.858}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{school of neuroanthropology, the second one stresses the plasticity of the brain and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{434.403}{442.982}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{argues that many neural structures can be shaped and influenced by idiosyncratic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{449.096}{90.482}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{cultural patterns.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{475.219}{442.974}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{It seems that your own work belongs to the first school of neuroanthropology. What}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{489.912}{442.868}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{makes you think the human brain is best described as endowed with innate and fixed}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{504.373}{442.859}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{structures rather than plastic ones? Your writings speak very highly of the biogenetic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{519.067}{442.869}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{structuralist school, but what is your view on the "culturalist" school of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{533.527}{442.870}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{neuroanthropology? Is your theoretical approach completely at odds with the latter or}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{548.221}{213.541}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{do you share at least some of their views?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{574.281}{440.496}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{First I would say that the cross-cultural principles, even universals, of magico-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{590.840}{443.660}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{religious practices, especially shamanism, speak to some underlying biological}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{607.400}{443.716}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{factors that produce these similarities. Certainly the physical and social}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{623.726}{443.700}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{environment provide influences, but I think the notion of cross-culturally}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{640.286}{443.636}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{distributed principles of shamanism, religion, meditation and spirituality speaks}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{656.846}{385.890}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{strongly to the underlying biological bases as the structural foundations.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{684.834}{443.802}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{In terms of the neuroanthropology traditions, my work has been largely focused}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{701.393}{443.671}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{within the first school, understanding religious and spiritual universals within the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{717.953}{443.605}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{biogenetic structuralist and neurognostic approaches. But I also think it abundantly}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{734.279}{443.699}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{clear that the brain is a highly plastic organ. At the same time, what is subject to}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}
\end{tikzpicture}

\noindent\begin{tikzpicture}[remember picture,overlay,x=1bp,y=1bp,shift={(current page.north west)}]

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{47}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.223}{443.642}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{plasticity are the innate tendencies, the extent to which they are elicited, suppressed}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{97.550}{443.678}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{or developed. So to me they are not opposing ideas, but different points of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{114.109}{443.639}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{departure. The innate modular structures are part of our deep primate heritage,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{130.669}{443.688}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{their slow manifestations across the primate and hominid and hominin lines speaks}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{147.229}{72.783}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{to accretion.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{175.217}{443.744}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{While I have primarily focused on the first neuroanthropology approach as a tool to}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{191.776}{443.915}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{explain universals, my own work has also addressed this notion of cultural and social}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{208.103}{443.685}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{effects on plasticity. This is exemplified in my research (for a summary, see:}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{224.662}{443.798}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Winkelman, 2018b) on the sociophysiological and psychological dynamics of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{241.222}{443.593}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{possession states. In this context I have made my clearest statements regarding the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{257.548}{443.679}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{roles of social circumstances in shaping plasticity of the brain into a very specific}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{274.108}{443.699}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{alteration of consciousness found cross-culturally and subsumed under various}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{290.668}{443.706}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{forms of possession. Some of my earliest research reflects concerns with the social}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{306.994}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{effects on plasticity of innate responses. In a study of the effects of formal education}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{323.554}{443.692}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{on extra sensory perception and of the effects of socialization on the manifestations}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{339.880}{443.746}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{of psi (Winkelman, 1982), I address issues related to how socialization affects}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{356.440}{443.763}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{experience and awareness of the world, very much concerned with the plasticity of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{372.999}{97.680}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{innate capacities.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{400.988}{443.702}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{So this plasticity is why cultural spiritual traditions are so important. They can take}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{417.547}{443.725}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{various disturbances in life, such as illness, injury, abandonment, being orphaned,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{434.107}{443.667}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{etc. and shape the body-mind response, using the consequences of these disturbances}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{450.433}{443.741}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{to alter the overall normal cognitive-emotional developmental trajectory of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{466.993}{443.562}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{person. Such disturbances, especially illness, are used in the traditions of shamanism}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{483.552}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{and meditation, taking the disturbance in normal development to enable one to}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{499.879}{443.660}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{engage our innate structures and develop and associate them in different ways than}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{516.438}{443.836}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{that normally intended by the unfolding of our nature and the cultural evolution of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{532.998}{443.716}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{our varied capacities. The shaman is a master in engaging, combining, integrating}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{549.324}{443.671}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the various modular structures, while the meditator is adept at stimulating, totally}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{565.884}{443.599}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{isolating and disenabling innate mental structures, leading to experiences of pure}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{582.444}{212.752}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{light, love and joy, or void/nothingness.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{610.494}{442.846}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{A good example of your biogenetic structuralist take on various cultural phenomena is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{624.955}{442.893}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{your theory of shamanism. According to you, the main features of shamanism are to be}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{639.649}{442.873}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{understood in terms of innate neurobiological structures ("neurognostic structures")}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{654.109}{442.937}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{present in every human: "The cross-cultural manifestations of basic experiences}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{668.803}{442.798}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{related to shamanism (e.g., soul flight, death-and-rebirth, animal identities) illustrates}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{683.263}{443.091}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{that these practices are not strictly cultural but are structured by underlying,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{697.957}{442.869}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{biologically inherent structures. These are neurobiological structures of knowing that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{712.418}{442.857}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{provide the universal aspects of the human brain/mind" (Winkelman, 2010a, p. 38; and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{727.112}{442.859}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{also: Winkelman, 2002b, 2002a). Yet, drawing upon Åke Hultkrantz's work you also}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{741.572}{442.877}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{acknowledge that shamanism arises out of environmental adaptations: "The worldwide}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.286}{442.846}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{similarity in shamans derives from the psychobiological bases of human consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{95.746}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{and its adaptation to social and ecological conditions of hunter-gatherer societies"}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{110.440}{139.601}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(Winkelman, 2010a, p. 64).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{136.562}{442.994}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Regarding the study of shamanism, is the model you endorse one in which neurognostic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{151.256}{442.760}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{structures directly cause specific cultural traits to emerge, or one with an interactionist}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{165.717}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{twist where cultural traits emerge from the interplay of neurognostic and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{180.410}{142.267}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{environmental constraints?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{206.470}{443.746}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{All of genetics and innate capacities unfold in interaction with the environment. I}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{223.030}{443.682}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{see the foraging band structure with a fission-fusion dynamic as the environment in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{239.589}{443.694}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{which shamanism emerged, something deep in hominin prehistory (Winkelman,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{255.916}{443.675}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{2010b). These ideas about the commonalities in chimp and hominin rituals emerged}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{272.475}{443.710}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{in my work circa with the second edition of Shamanism (2010a). These ancient ritual}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{289.035}{359.129}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{structures reflect what is at issue in the first statements you review.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{317.023}{443.737}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{The second issue about the effects of foraging environments on the manifestation of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{333.583}{443.684}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{shamanism is more related to the contrast with other kinds of magico-religious}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{349.909}{443.676}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{practitioners (Winkelman, 1990). I think that many of these same capacities at the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{366.469}{443.721}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{core of shamanism are manifested in the experiences and behavior of possession cult}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{383.028}{443.589}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{mediums, whose distinctive features emerged from the formative influences exerted}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{399.355}{443.677}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{by the oppressive societal dynamics of social stratification and political integration,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{415.915}{433.766}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{probably exacerbated by patrilineal social structures and compromised nutrition.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{444.136}{443.564}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{So I think that the traits emerge both from the innate tendencies, as well as}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{460.462}{443.702}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{environmental provocation. For instance, the altered state of consciousness (ASC)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{477.022}{443.550}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{associated with extreme fasting also emerge "naturally" from the effects of food}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{493.582}{443.693}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{shortage and short-term starvation. I think the evidence indicates that out-of-body}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{509.908}{443.670}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{experiences can be provoked by many stressors, including accidents, long-distance}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{526.468}{443.773}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{running, etc. I emphasize these in the sense of a neurognostic structure, something}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{543.027}{443.659}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{innate about how we perceive the world. The cultural part is what we believe about}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{559.354}{443.693}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{these experiences. Such cultural beliefs may have many sources apart from the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{575.913}{416.352}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{neurognostic dynamics produced by the innate dynamics of these experiences.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{134.561}{604.086}{24.676}{ALIUSC7F7F7F}{\ALIUSFontCormorantLight}{46.647}{\ALIUSPullQuoteOpen}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{621.490}{309.122}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{I think that the traits emerge both from the innate}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{471.118}{638.838}{13.761}{ALIUSC7F7F7F}{\ALIUSFontCormorantLight}{46.647}{\ALIUSPullQuoteClose}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{638.982}{304.067}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{tendencies, as well as environmental provocation.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{688.565}{443.659}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{This distinction of neurognostic versus cultural structures raises the question of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{705.125}{443.862}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{extent to which shamanic traditions depend on culture. Clearly cultural loss leads}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{721.685}{443.825}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{to loss of shamanic practices, but whether this is simply the consequence of some}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{738.011}{443.680}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{loss of "knowledge" or some broader consequences of cultural disintegration is not}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

\noindent\begin{tikzpicture}[remember picture,overlay,x=1bp,y=1bp,shift={(current page.north west)}]
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-65.268bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.233bp);
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-777.332bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.466bp);
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{49}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.223}{443.640}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{clear. To me, the remarkable similarities of shamanic practices in societies around}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{97.550}{443.747}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the world speaks to something innate about the fundamental dynamic of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{114.109}{443.697}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{shamanism, something that can emerge from innate cognitive, social and emotional}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{130.669}{443.739}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{tendencies rather than something sustained primarily through cultural belief; this is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{146.995}{440.496}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{supported by converging evidence from ethology, neuropsychology and cross-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{163.555}{443.671}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{cultural studies (Winkelman, 2010c). However, when these tendencies are provoked}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{180.115}{443.697}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{in the modern world, their sequela and consequences are quite different from that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{196.441}{443.728}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{seen under conditions of foraging societies because the formative social influences}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{213.001}{443.697}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(and cultural beliefs) are dramatically different. The environment is also a factor}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{229.560}{443.720}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{here, where animals are clearly central to adaptation and survival, whether as food}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{245.887}{443.735}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{or predators, or even as sentinels. I think that a core part of shamanism was a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{262.446}{443.628}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{relationship with the world of animals on so many levels. This gets reduced to cows}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{279.006}{443.676}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{and chickens and later dogs and cats. Not as complex animal-based environmental}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{295.332}{443.756}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{relations that creates identities and powers and channels into nature typical of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{311.892}{97.802}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{foraging societies.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{339.943}{442.880}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{According to you, shamanic concepts such as the belief in a "traveling soul" or in "soul}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{354.636}{163.414}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{flight" are to be explained by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{244.290}{354.636}{76.792}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{innate modules}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{321.096}{354.636}{199.328}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(Winkelman, 2002b, 2002a, 2010a,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{369.097}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{2017b). The concept of a module has been largely debated and what is meant by it in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{383.791}{442.922}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Fodor's seminal piece (Fodor, 1983) is very different from what is meant in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{398.484}{356.973}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{contemporary evolutionary psychology (C. Barrett \& Kurzban, 2006).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{424.607}{442.838}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{What definition of a module do you endorse? For example, do you take automaticity and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{439.067}{442.868}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{informational encapsulation to be definitional of what a module is? Moreover, do you}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{453.761}{443.097}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{think with Fodor that the modularity of the mind is restricted to perception and does}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{468.221}{442.868}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{not concern cognition (reasoning, concepts, etc.); or, along with Tooby \& Cosmides}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{482.915}{442.863}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(1992), Sperber (1996a) and others, do you champion the massive modularity}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{497.609}{304.168}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hypothesis (the view that the mind is modular throughout)?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{523.669}{443.749}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{My conceptualization of innate modules is primarily informed by Gardner's work,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{540.228}{443.591}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{as well as the broader concept of innate operators used by d'Aquili to conceptualize}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{556.555}{443.685}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{universals of spiritual experience. These innate modules or operators are far more}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{573.114}{443.679}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{than perceptual devices, but engage full-blown cognitive processes providing the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{589.674}{443.682}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{basis for innate intelligences. I see shamanism as exploiting a variety of these innate}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{606.000}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{intelligences, and furthermore using ritual processes to combine innate}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{622.560}{443.683}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{intelligences, for instance in animal allies that combine the interpersonal and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{638.886}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{naturalistic intelligences. This integration of (1) interpersonal intelligence—a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{655.446}{443.774}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{capacity for a "theory of mind" to infer others' mental processes and to work}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{672.006}{443.637}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{effectively with others through an understanding of their motivations and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{688.332}{443.660}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{intentions; with (2) the naturalist intelligence that provides "expertise in the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{704.892}{443.696}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{recognition and classification of the numerous species—the flora and fauna—of his}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{721.451}{443.682}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{or her environment" (Gardner, 2000, p. 36). This cross-modular integration is in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{737.778}{443.673}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{contrast to the normal isolated function of modules. It also provides a new capacity}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{358.539}{443.709}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{-An existential intelligence that reflects the cognitive aspects manifested in the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{374.865}{443.585}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{spiritual intelligence, "an ability to locate oneself with respect to the furthest reaches}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{391.425}{443.629}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{of the cosmos […] the significance of life, the meaning of death […] a concern with}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{450.729}{10.452}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{87.537}{450.729}{56.120}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{experiential}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{143.658}{450.729}{69.814}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{—rather than}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{212.923}{450.729}{53.131}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{conceptual}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{266.043}{450.729}{15.515}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{or}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{280.991}{450.729}{40.024}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{doxastic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{321.010}{450.729}{199.522}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{: it consists of out-of-body experiences,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{465.189}{442.857}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{near death experiences, astral projection experiences, etc. (e.g., Winkelman, 2010a, p.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{479.883}{176.547}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{117). Now, you argue that these}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{256.166}{479.883}{56.032}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{experiences}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{312.209}{479.883}{173.301}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{somewhat automatically trigger}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{487.489}{479.883}{30.682}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{beliefs}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{494.344}{442.975}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{whose content largely depends on the content of experience. This line of reasoning}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{509.037}{442.918}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{looks very much like that of Tylor (1871) when he suggests that beliefs in souls are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{523.498}{442.889}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{triggered by altered states of consciousness such as dreaming. Yet, the relationship}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{538.192}{442.855}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{between experience and beliefs (or concepts) is far from simple and obvious. Unless one}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{552.652}{442.970}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{endorses the view that perceiving is believing—this view seems wrong to me, since one}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{567.346}{442.823}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{can perceive things without taking them to be real (Dokic \& Martin, 2012; Fortier,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{581.807}{442.835}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{2018a, 2018b)—it is obvious that some dissociation is to be found between experience}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{596.500}{440.521}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{and belief: (1) some people will believe in soul flight without experiencing any out-of-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{610.961}{442.873}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{body experience; (2) and some will experience out-of-body experiences without}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{625.655}{290.107}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{believing in soul flights. Let me illustrate both (1) and (2).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{651.777}{442.642}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(1) During my fieldwork in the Middle Ucayali (Peruvian Amazon), a Shipibo friend of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{666.471}{328.538}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{mine once told me about the experience he had of losing his soul (}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{406.203}{666.471}{22.778}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{kaya}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{428.985}{666.471}{91.471}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{). While my friend}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{680.931}{442.886}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{was quietly paddling, his canoe suddenly capsized and he fell into the river. He managed}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{695.625}{442.938}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{to put the canoe back in its straight position and came back home but noticed he was}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{710.085}{442.857}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{feeling strange: he was feeling very depressed. Intriguingly, he interpreted this feeling}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{724.779}{440.521}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{as his soul being gone. As a side note, it should be stressed that according to the Shipibo-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{739.240}{442.962}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Konibo model of the person, when your soul is gone, you do not become a zombie or an}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{366.998}{442.860}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{As these two examples demonstrate, it is not obvious that religious beliefs or concepts}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{381.458}{418.386}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{can be explained strictly by the activation of modules whose output is experiential:}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{495.791}{381.458}{24.722}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{such}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{396.152}{442.951}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{beliefs can be held without the module being activated; and the module can be triggered}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{410.613}{160.422}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{without such beliefs being formed}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{238.056}{410.613}{282.490}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{. What is your take on this? How do you conceive of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{425.306}{282.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{relationship between experiential modules and beliefs?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{451.366}{443.755}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{I think that it is important to make the distinction between, on one hand, the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{467.926}{443.653}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{structural and functional aspects of the experience, and on the other hand the}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{517.371}{443.688}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{metaphysical concepts may be very neurognostic (Winkelman, 2013) or they may be}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{533.931}{443.616}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{formed by a variety of cultural traditions and assumptions. This would include the}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{52}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.223}{443.652}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{distance running, etc.—indicates we are seeing something about the structural}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{97.550}{443.651}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{features of the organism's perceptual/conceptual capacities. I see in the OBE first}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{114.109}{443.677}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the disassembling of the normal integration of different modular structures—visual}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{130.669}{443.700}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{field, body sense, egoic identity—and then subsequently the emergence of a deep}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{146.995}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{and ancient self-structure, perhaps related to the mimetic mind (Winkelman, 2017b)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{163.555}{323.972}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{or one of the non-verbal forms of self identified by Damasio.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{191.776}{443.620}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{How we understand—even perceive and relate to—these experiences depends on our}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{208.103}{443.620}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{prior orientation. In the context of an animistic pre-modern worldview the spiritual}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{224.662}{443.649}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{dimensions and explanations of these experiences is natural and predominant. When}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{241.222}{443.574}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{you take post-modern science students into a lab, of course their explanations will}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{257.548}{443.656}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{be different. But furthermore don't think for a moment that those who "participate}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{274.108}{443.656}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{in experiments where neuroscientists purposely induce out-of-body experiences" are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{290.668}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{really experiencing the same thing as a shaman who just collapsed after drumming}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{306.994}{443.628}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{and dancing for six hours, or someone lost in an ayahuasca journey, or someone}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{323.554}{443.710}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{clinically dead and laying on the side of the rode with paramedics working to}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{339.880}{443.712}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{stimulate a heartbeat. There are many dimensions to the dynamics of the OBE}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{356.440}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{besides some simple phenomenological descriptions about body and self-awareness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{372.999}{70.864}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{and identity.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{401.050}{440.521}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{It is not entirely clear to me what the explanatory gain is to resort to psycho-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{415.744}{442.807}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{evolutionary accounts of cognitive/cultural phenomena. To illustrate my skepticism, let}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{430.204}{442.815}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{me take the example of a psycho-evolutionary account of the fusiform face area (FFA).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{444.898}{442.832}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{The FFA has been discussed in evolutionary terms both by yourself (Winkelman,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{459.359}{443.021}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{2018a, p. 6) and by other evolutionary psychologists/cognitive anthropologists}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{474.052}{442.865}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(Sperber \& Hirschfeld, 2004, pp. 40–42). Specifically, in "An ontology of psychedelic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{488.513}{442.861}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{entity experiences in evolutionary psychology and neurophenomenology," you propose}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{503.207}{442.887}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{that the reason why people hallucinate many eyes and faces under the effect of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{517.667}{442.810}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{psychedelic compounds is that their FFA becomes hyper-activated (Winkelman, 2018a,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{532.361}{442.872}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{p. 7). But what is the actual "added value" of arguing that the FFA has been}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{546.821}{442.927}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{evolutionarily-shaped? Some evidence suggests the FFA is in fact not evolutionarily}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{561.515}{442.816}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{shaped, but depends on expertise: it is an expertise-dedicated area (Gauthier \& Nelson,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{575.976}{442.847}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{2001). This explains why experts in nonface objects (e.g., cars) have the FFA activated}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{590.669}{442.887}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{by objects other than faces. If Gauthier's theory of the FFA is correct, this means that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{605.130}{442.864}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{those who have the FFA being activated by faces are "face experts" and that their FFA}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{619.824}{442.888}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{"module" has been shaped by expertise rather evolution. The point worth stressing is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{634.284}{442.875}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{that one can still say (a) "hallucinations featuring multiple faces correlate with the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{648.978}{442.822}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hyper-activity of the FFA," even if the FFA turns out to be shaped through}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{663.439}{442.860}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{development—rather than through evolution. This is what I mean when I say that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{678.132}{442.841}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{evolutionary explanations bring no "explanatory added value." Another way to put this}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{692.593}{442.863}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{objection would be to take the example of cars. Gauthier has shown that the FFA could}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{707.287}{442.876}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{become a "module" specialized in car detection. Now, no one would claim that we have}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{721.747}{443.074}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{a car module that has been shaped through evolution because obviously cars did not}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{736.441}{442.868}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{exist in the Pleistocene. Yet, it is still possible to propose that (b) "hallucinations}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}
\end{tikzpicture}

  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-65.268bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.233bp);
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-777.332bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.466bp);
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{53}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.286}{442.847}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{featuring multiple cars correlate with the hyper-activity of the FFA (or any other brain}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{95.746}{442.818}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{area(s) specialized in the detection of cars)." At the end of the day, it seems that the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{110.440}{442.847}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{explanatory merit of statements such as (a) or (b) lie not in the appeal to some putative}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{124.901}{394.789}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{evolutionary origin—neither (a) nor (b) do such a thing—but simply in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{476.684}{124.901}{41.484}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{reducing}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{139.594}{442.855}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{phenomenology to some brain function. In other words, the explanatory added-value}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{154.288}{394.678}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{of such statements comes from reducing cognitive functions to brain activity.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{180.410}{442.849}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{What is true of the FFA is true of most—if not of all—modules. Their evolutionary origin}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{194.871}{442.966}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{is very controversial and some authors have shown that modules can be accounted for}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{209.565}{440.521}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{by developmental mechanisms rather than evolution (Elman et al., 1996; Karmiloff-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{224.025}{442.864}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Smith, 1992, 2009). When you argue that the "social cognition module," the "biological}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{238.719}{442.816}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{module," the "physical module," etc. explain crucial aspects of shamanism, the claim}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{253.179}{442.800}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{seems to be that your evolutionary account sheds some light on the phenomenon at}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{267.873}{442.965}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hand. But it can be objected that the same could be said even if all our modules have}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{282.334}{442.849}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{been shaped by development and have nothing to do with evolution. For example, you}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{297.028}{442.880}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{can say "people anthropomorphize their surroundings because of the social cognition}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{311.488}{442.942}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{module", even if it turns out this module is not an adapted function (i.e., is not shaped by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{326.182}{442.795}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{evolution); even if evolutionary processes are not involved, it will always remain that we}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{340.642}{442.929}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{have cognitive functions specialized in processing social stimuli and that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{355.336}{442.848}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{anthropomorphism can always be attributed to them. In short, according to you, what}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{370.030}{390.675}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{is the real explanatory gain of evolutionary accounts of cultural phenomena?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{396.090}{443.722}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{I think that the evolution of function is what is the focus of selection, and that this}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{412.416}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{always happens through repurposing old hardware. So the FFA undoubtedly faced}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{428.976}{443.665}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{many selective pressures, one of which is its detection of faces. The point here about}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{445.535}{443.682}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the innate modules is that they were designed to provide a certain functional}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{461.862}{440.457}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{response. My approach is not to say that the responses are just about the brain—}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{478.421}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{obviously they are stimulated by social and environmental context. New function}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{494.981}{333.932}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{can emerge out of new connections rather than new hardware.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{522.969}{443.559}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{The importance of the innate modules and evolved psychology approaches is the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{539.529}{443.759}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{following. When we find recurrent patterns of experience or behavior across}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{556.088}{443.634}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{cultures, the traditional cultural explanation of religious or spiritual beliefs offers}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{572.415}{443.618}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{no explanatory power. Why is an out-of-body experience reported around the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{588.974}{443.757}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{world? Not because cultures believe this, but because of innate dispositions. When}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{605.534}{443.611}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{we encounter universals or highly repeated phenomena across cultures, there must}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{621.860}{443.716}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{be a biological reason. Now notably we do not have people from cultures around the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{638.420}{443.661}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{world reporting the presence of cars, not even cars staring at them (which one might}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{654.746}{443.690}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{even expect since the two headlights are like eyes and the grill like a big mouthed}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{671.306}{443.628}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{grin!). So is it as you say "[T]he explanatory added-value of such statements comes}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{687.866}{443.671}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{from reducing cognitive functions to brain activity"? To me, that is a basic function}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{704.192}{443.599}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{of neurognostic approaches in explaining religious universals. It has to do with how}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{720.752}{443.595}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{our brain operates. Of course there is the added question of how it is that religious,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}
\end{tikzpicture}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{276.503}{442.823}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{If cultural phenomena studied by anthropologists—e.g., animistic and totemistic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{290.963}{443.004}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{beliefs/practices—are in fact underpinned by universal adapted functions, one may}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{305.657}{442.859}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{then wonder how psycho-evolutionary explanations can make sense of the}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{334.811}{442.901}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{totemists everywhere in the world and to the same degree (e.g., Descola, 2013; Ingold,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{349.272}{442.866}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{2000; Testart, 2012). If cognitive adapted functions—such as the social cognition}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{595.738}{443.701}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{expressed in why our cars have problems, why the computer doesn't work, why the}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{628.624}{443.663}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{capacity is expressed in everyone and everywhere to the same degree. Obviously}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{645.184}{443.679}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{social circumstances can elicit or repress certain tendencies. But is there a culture}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{678.070}{346.136}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{emotions, tendencies, social relations? I don't think so. Show me.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{423.772}{678.408}{11.404}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontSymbolFallback}{13.528}{J}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{706.291}{440.496}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{However, our metaphysical world is less animist and totemist, etc. than many pre-}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{739.177}{443.897}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{environment. When you live in a culture where the traditions of your ancestors still}

\noindent\begin{tikzpicture}[remember picture,overlay,x=1bp,y=1bp,shift={(current page.north west)}]
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-65.268bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.233bp);
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-777.332bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.466bp);
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{55}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.223}{443.708}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{organize your day to day, monthly and seasonal activities, such as in agriculture, the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{97.550}{443.769}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{compulsion to follow your ancestors' advice is very strong and probably adaptive.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{114.109}{443.678}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Ancestor worship is an adaptive way of maintaining vital traditions and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{130.669}{443.660}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{mediumistic communication with them to get advice on how to address problems}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{146.995}{443.651}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{is probably an adaptation for accessing the knowledge of our collective memories.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{163.555}{443.740}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{But when we live in cultures where the traditions of our ancestors, including their}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{180.115}{443.722}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{work skills, habits and beliefs, are totally irrelevant to our day to day adaptations,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{196.674}{288.287}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{small surprise that ancestor worship is not important.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{224.662}{443.713}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Ditto for animism. I think that it is not possible to fully experience nature and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{241.222}{443.731}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{perceive its animistic qualities unless one is immersed in it, solely and far from}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{257.548}{443.621}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{civilization. When we live in intimate relations with nature, our sense of animism}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{274.108}{443.683}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{also must shift. After all there are all kinds of non-human living things and natural}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{290.668}{189.024}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{forces to be experienced in nature.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{318.656}{443.729}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{So the ways in which the innate modules are elicited, their cross-entrainments with}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{335.215}{443.678}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{other modules and cognitive process, and their roles in culture produce a lot of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{351.542}{443.725}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{variation. Shamanism provided traditions for engaging and elevating certain aspects}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{368.101}{443.721}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{of consciousness adaptive for our foraging ancestors and their relations to nature.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{384.661}{146.495}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Back to the plasticity issue.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{134.561}{412.834}{24.676}{ALIUSC7F7F7F}{\ALIUSFontCormorantLight}{46.647}{\ALIUSPullQuoteOpen}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{430.238}{302.274}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{[T]he ways in which the innate modules are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{447.730}{302.304}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{elicited, their cross-entrainments with other}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{465.223}{302.292}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{modules and cognitive process, and their roles in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{482.715}{302.223}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{culture produce a lot of variation. Shamanism}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{500.208}{302.268}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{provided traditions for engaging and elevating}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{517.701}{302.127}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{certain aspects of consciousness adaptive for our}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{459.690}{534.815}{13.761}{ALIUSC7F7F7F}{\ALIUSFontCormorantLight}{46.647}{\ALIUSPullQuoteClose}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{535.193}{293.252}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{foraging ancestors and their relations to nature.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{580.874}{442.776}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{You have been a pioneer in using databases to address big anthropological questions.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{595.334}{442.916}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{In particular, you have investigated the relationship between economic systems, social}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{610.028}{442.768}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{structures, and types of magico-religious practitioners (priests, shamans, healers, etc.).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{624.488}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Rather than theorizing about these variables on the basis of a single fieldwork, as many}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{639.182}{443.109}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{anthropologists do, you looked at the Human Relations Area Files (HRAF), gathered the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{653.643}{442.844}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{relevant data, and resorted to statistical tools to answer the questions you were}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{668.336}{419.886}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{interested in. This led to some groundbreaking findings (Winkelman, 1986, 1992).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{694.459}{442.685}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{In recent years, several large projects have similarly tried to address big questions}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{709.153}{442.994}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{about religion by resorting to databases. The two most significant of them are certainly}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{723.613}{442.822}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the SESHAT database (seshatdatabank.info) and the Database of Religious History}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{738.307}{343.416}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(religiondatabase.org). What do you think of those recent projects?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}
\end{tikzpicture}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{56}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.286}{442.872}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Strikingly, the questions tackled by recent dataset-based research programs}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{95.746}{442.738}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{completely overlook the topic of altered states of consciousness. Do you think big data}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{110.440}{442.914}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{could significantly help shed new light on altered states of consciousness or are there}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{124.901}{442.857}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{intrinsic limitations to this method? In your recent work, you do not use databases}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{139.594}{348.190}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{anymore; but are you planning to use such tools again in the future?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{165.654}{443.675}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{While I used some data from the HRAF for my research, my research was based on}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{182.214}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{a subsample from the Standard Cross-cultural Sample. There are some subtle}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{198.773}{443.616}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{differences between them. I feel that it is unfortunate that anthropologists and other}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{215.100}{443.676}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{social scientists don't rely more on cross-cultural data to address questions regarding}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{231.659}{443.677}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{social and cultural universals and social evolution of phenomena, religious or}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{248.219}{443.689}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{otherwise. Such data is essential for more valid generalizations. So it is good to see}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{264.545}{443.665}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{new data sets being developed to bring empirical data to address questions about}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{281.105}{443.688}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the cultural evolution of religion. Eventually we will need both synchronic and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{297.431}{443.648}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{diachronic data sets, and the significance of having a pinpointed culture and time}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{313.991}{443.695}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{for valid synchronic analysis may not be incorporated into some efforts. How we}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{330.551}{378.366}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{can incorporate such different info into a single data set is challenging.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{358.539}{443.674}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{From some of the earliest cross-cultural research on magico-religious practitioners}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{375.099}{443.619}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(e.g., Bourguignon \& Evascu, 1977), the cross-cultural variation in the alteration of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{391.658}{443.688}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{consciousness has been a significant area of research and theory. Briefly,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{407.985}{443.686}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Bourguignon was the first to report empirical data on the association of possession}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{424.544}{443.610}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{ASC with more complex societies. My subsequent research, building on her}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{441.104}{443.648}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{concepts, has shown that possession appears as the predominant socially recognized}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{457.430}{443.770}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{ASC under conditions of political complexity and the associated conditions of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{473.990}{440.496}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{oppression of females. To me, this is one of the important contributions of cross-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{490.549}{443.675}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{cultural research in general, and specifically with respect to the issue of innate}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{506.876}{443.640}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{modules. One of the arguments against a cross-cultural shamanism is that ASC are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{523.435}{443.809}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{not expressed the same everywhere. True. But what explains the patterns of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{539.762}{443.667}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{variation? This is where cross-cultural research can help us understand how a set of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{556.322}{443.752}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{innate capacities, in this case for alterations of consciousness, may be expressed in a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{572.881}{273.634}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{variety of forms, depending on local circumstance.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{600.869}{443.667}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{My cross-cultural data base on magico-religious practitioners and altered states of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{617.429}{443.672}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{consciousness is a bit of a paradox. On one hand, its initial formulation provided}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{633.989}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the basis for my dissertation, Shamans, Priests and Witches, a variety of articles, and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{650.315}{443.559}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{most importantly my career of developing concepts regarding the universal}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{666.875}{443.682}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{biological bases of shamanism. After I finished my dissertation, I received a National}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{683.434}{443.621}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Science Foundation Dissertation Improvement Grant and I completely}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{699.761}{443.651}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{reformulated the variables based on the experience of the dissertation, recoded the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{716.320}{443.554}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{data, and did coding reliability checks. This new database was never analyzed (but}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{732.880}{443.620}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{is available from HRAF and on researchgate.net). For a variety of reasons my career}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}
\end{tikzpicture}
