\noindent\begin{tikzpicture}[remember picture,overlay,x=1bp,y=1bp,shift={(current page.north west)}]
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-65.268bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.233bp);
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-777.332bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.466bp);
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{57}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.223}{443.671}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{took some different directions (neurotheology, cross-cultural relations, medical}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{97.550}{443.713}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{anthropology, psychedelics) and I never returned to analyze the new data, or for that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{114.109}{390.407}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{matter, many of the obvious questions suggested by the original data set.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{142.331}{443.716}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Will I return to analyze the data? I think about it from time to time, but I generally}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{158.657}{443.680}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{feel like I am too old to want to go learn how to use another statistical package. I}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{175.217}{400.434}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{hope someone will discover this unanalyzed data and do something with it.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{203.438}{443.696}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Principal areas that might be addressed? (1) the evolution of priesthoods. What are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{219.764}{443.680}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the origins in ancestor worship and what are the factors that contribute to their}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{236.324}{443.669}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{emergence as dominant ritual structures of society epitomizing the features of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{252.884}{443.681}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{religions and priests? (2) ASC and healing: Are different types of ASCs associated}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{269.210}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{with different illness ideologies?; How does this data set relate to Murdock's data on}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{285.770}{309.497}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Theories of Illness (Murdock, Wilson, \& Frederick, 1980)?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{313.820}{442.877}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{The Cognitive Science of Religion (J. L. Barrett, 2000, 2007; Pyysiäinen, 2013) is one of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{328.514}{442.995}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the most ambitious programs of naturalization of religion. Although this research}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{342.975}{442.856}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{program has made some important findings, it has consistently overlooked the role}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{357.668}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{experience—and especially altered consciousness—plays in religion. For example, it has}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{372.129}{442.834}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{been argued that conscious experience is uninteresting because it has no effect on}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{386.823}{442.867}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{religious concepts. That is, the same religious concepts will be formed whether or not}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{401.283}{442.889}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{altered states of consciousness are experienced (e.g., Boyer, 2001, Chapter 9; Cohen,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{415.977}{36.567}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{2007).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{442.099}{442.865}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{In your HRAF-based work on magico-religious practitioners, you have demonstrated}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{456.793}{442.867}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{that the type of practitioner found in a culture largely depends on modes of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{471.254}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{consciousness entertained in that culture (Winkelman, 1986, 1992). Namely, the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{485.947}{442.845}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{"integrative mode of consciousness" is only found in cultures where magico-religious}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{500.408}{442.863}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{practitioners are shamans, healers, and mediums but not in cultures where these}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{515.102}{442.875}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{practitioners are sorcerers, witches, or priests. This finding seems to provide a strong}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{529.562}{443.032}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{argument in favor of the view that religious concepts are to a certain extent shaped by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{544.256}{114.487}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{conscious experience.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{570.378}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{However, this argument works only if we can establish what the direction of causality}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{585.072}{442.829}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{is between magico-religious practitioner types and the integrative mode of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{599.532}{442.873}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{consciousness. A first possibility is that most of the traits defining shamans, healers, and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{614.226}{442.880}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{mediums are determined by the integrative mode of consciousness. But a second}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{628.687}{442.826}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{possibility is that most of their traits coalesce as a result of other factors (e.g., biosocial}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{643.380}{442.919}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{or socioeconomic factors) and subsequently cause the emergence of rituals inducing}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{657.841}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the integrative mode of consciousness. According to this account, the integrative mode}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{672.535}{442.835}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{of consciousness would be the effect and not the cause of the traits defining shamans,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{687.228}{268.564}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{healers, and mediums and their idiosyncratic beliefs.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{713.351}{442.742}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Which of these accounts do you think is the most accurate? More broadly, your work}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{727.811}{442.982}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{on magico-religious practitioners posits three main variables: the biosocial function, the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{742.505}{442.976}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{mode of consciousness (which is sometimes described as a biosocial function) and the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}
\end{tikzpicture}

\noindent\begin{tikzpicture}[remember picture,overlay,x=1bp,y=1bp,shift={(current page.north west)}]
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-65.268bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.233bp);
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-777.332bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.466bp);
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{58}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.286}{442.853}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{socioeconomic condition. But what is the causal role of each of these variables in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{95.980}{304.314}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{bringing about specific magico-religious practitioner types?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{122.039}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Three bases of magico-religious practice reflect the fundamental impulses}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{138.366}{443.611}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{underlying religious life. The cross-cultural distribution of these institutionalized}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{154.925}{443.699}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{practices reveals that the fundamental forms of religious life are not arbitrary or}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{171.485}{443.728}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{simply cultural, but derived from biogenetic human impulses that are manifested}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{187.811}{443.629}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{across cultures and time, albeit modified in their manifestations by the reigning}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{204.371}{234.071}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{subsistence, social and political conditions.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{232.592}{443.714}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{These cross-cultural commonalities are also manifested in the configurations of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{248.919}{443.647}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{magico-religious practitioners. Societies in the sample had specific typical patterns}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{265.478}{206.493}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{of co-occurrence of practitioner types.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{293.700}{411.209}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{1. Practitioner: Shaman or other Healer Complex (Shaman/Healer or Healer)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{321.688}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{2. Practitioners: Priest and Healer Complex or Medium (1 society with two Healer}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{338.247}{55.681}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Complex)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{366.469}{388.380}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{3. Practitioners: Priest, Healer Complex, and Medium or Sorcerer/Witch}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{394.690}{323.008}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{4. Practitioners: Priest, Healer, Medium and Sorcerer/Witch}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{422.678}{443.664}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{In order to reveal these underlying biogenetic functions, entailment analyses were}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{439.005}{440.496}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{used to identify the relationship between the formal functions of these magico-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{455.564}{443.662}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{religious practitioner types and the processes for practitioner role selection}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{472.124}{443.657}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(Winkelman, 1986). This revealed three major relationships between selection}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{488.450}{443.654}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{processes and magico-religious activities, notably the former entailing the latter}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{505.010}{121.054}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{rather than vice-versa.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{533.231}{443.716}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(1) Alteration of Consciousness and Healing. If there is selection for the role by (a)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{549.558}{443.804}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{signs from the spirits, involuntary illness or spontaneous visions or deliberate vision}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{566.117}{443.672}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{quests, then (b) there is further training involving alterations of consciousness, and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{582.677}{443.762}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(c) professional activities of healing and divination. These features were typically}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{599.003}{443.713}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{characteristic of the practitioners of the Healer Complex (all Shamans and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{615.563}{443.726}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Shaman/Healers and some of the Healers) and the Mediums. This is a human}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{632.123}{443.621}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{universal, manifested and utilized differently in different types of societies and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{648.449}{443.690}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{traditions. So your statement above that the integrative mode of consciousness is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{665.009}{443.805}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{not found in cultures where there are Sorcerer/Witches or Priests is mistaken. All}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{681.335}{443.680}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{societies, including those with Priests and Sorcerer/Witches, have the integrative}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{697.895}{443.589}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{mode of consciousness manifested in Shamans, Shaman/Healers, Healers or}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{714.454}{443.682}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Mediums. All societies have one of these shamanistic healers that exploit the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{731.014}{275.961}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{potentials of the integrative mode of consciousness.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{274.108}{443.685}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(3) Social Labeling and Malevolent Activities. If there was selection for the role on}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{356.440}{443.627}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Sorcerers/Witches. This negative dimension of the supernatural is produced}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{372.999}{443.692}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{through the persecutions carried out primarily by Priests and Healers, who}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{389.559}{235.077}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{designate people as being a Sorcerer/Witch.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{417.610}{442.829}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{In your work, you often argue that religious practices and institutions (e.g., shamanic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{432.070}{442.788}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{healing rituals) are deeply adaptive (Winkelman, 2009, Chapter 7 and 9, 2010a,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{446.764}{442.865}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Chapter 6; Winkelman \& Baker, 2010, Chapters 5, 6 and 11). Now, some cognitive}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{461.224}{442.867}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{scientists of religion have argued that religious practices and institutions consist mainly}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{490.379}{442.801}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{between adaptationism and spandrelism: Sosis, 2009). What are your main arguments}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{545.826}{444.764}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{I have three chapters in an upcoming book The Super-Natural after the Neuroturn}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{562.386}{443.675}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{that I summarize in the following paragraphs. The simple evidence against the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{578.712}{443.611}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{spandrel arguments is the many different functional and adaptive advantages of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{595.272}{443.777}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{diverse components of religious thought, as well as its group level effects. It is very}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{611.831}{443.661}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{easy to show the powerful social effects of supernatural assumptions, costly displays,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{628.158}{443.661}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{ingroup cognition, etc. Similarly, the psychological benefits from enhanced}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{644.717}{443.641}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{endorphins, anti-depressive effects, enhanced social support, etc. speak to a lot of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{661.277}{443.636}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{components of religious thought that facilitate human adaptation. Whether these}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{677.603}{443.724}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{are strictly biological or emerge in cultural-gene-environment interactions is really}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{694.163}{443.678}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{immaterial. The cognitive, social and physical environment is always part of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{710.723}{183.310}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{expression of genetic capabilities.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{738.711}{186.834}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{So why consider religion adaptive?}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.223}{443.676}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{When primatologists study animal ritual they don't debate whether or not the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{97.550}{443.659}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{rituals have adaptive functions. Why change the tune when we come to humans?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{114.109}{443.662}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Rituals exercise a variety of adaptive functions in moderating emotions,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{130.669}{443.677}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{psychological and social relations and cognitive processes. Human's supernatural}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{146.995}{443.727}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{behaviors involve exaptations of the functions of primates' ritualized displays that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{163.555}{443.610}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{were used to expand mechanisms for social communication and coordination as part}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{180.115}{443.650}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{of human innate psychosocial processes and cognitive structures. The}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{196.441}{443.738}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{communicative and integrative displays among primates, particularly the ritualized}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{213.001}{443.606}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{behaviors for group unification among great apes, provide a framework for}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{229.560}{443.673}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{understanding the origins of ritual behavior in activities that enhanced social}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{245.887}{443.632}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{integration. The concept of costly displays provides a framework for identifying the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{262.446}{443.747}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{forces that led to the shamanic expansion out of the hominid ritual capacity, using}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{279.006}{443.698}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{drumming, singing and dancing to expand social integration function provided by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{295.332}{443.661}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{mimesis. Shamanism emerged in this expansion of the mimetic capacity and its}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{311.892}{443.578}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{associated suite of expressive capacities that extended the social coordination}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{328.218}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{functions of displays. Shamanic rituals expanded as adaptations involving increased}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{344.778}{443.682}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{capacities for ritual bonding of communities and the associated enhanced}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{361.338}{223.772}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{endorphin and placebo healing responses.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{389.326}{443.526}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{The varied ways in which diverse alterations of consciousness contribute to healing}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{405.885}{443.666}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{attests to basic biological functions of this mode of consciousness. Shamanic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{422.445}{443.741}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{alterations of consciousness reflect the physiological effects of ritual practices in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{438.771}{443.802}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{stimulating the modulatory neurotransmitter systems of serotonin, dopamine and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{455.331}{443.706}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the endocannabinoids, as well as the endogenous opioid system. These provide the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{471.891}{443.688}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{biological bases for these experiences in an enhancement of the functioning of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{488.217}{443.529}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{neurotransmitter systems that enhance access to evolutionarily early strata of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{504.777}{443.696}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{brain. These brain areas provide the special cognitive qualities of consciousness that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{521.336}{443.661}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{underlie perceptions of the supernatural. Ritual practices induce supernatural}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{537.663}{443.688}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{experiences through disrupting higher order information integration and top-down}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{554.222}{443.670}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{cognitive control, permitting emergence of cognitive processes related to ancient}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{570.549}{443.699}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{brain structures and primary process levels of cognition, identity and awareness.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{587.108}{443.664}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Shamanic alterations of consciousness provide adaptations that enhance cognition}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{603.668}{443.740}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{through expanded access to unconscious mental processes and the ability to}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{619.995}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{integrate the global brain dynamics, rather than just the habitual networks (i.e.,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{636.554}{443.623}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{default mode network). The effects of psychedelics on global brain dynamics shows}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{653.114}{443.764}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{an enhanced global connectivity and increased connectivity between areas that are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{669.440}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{not normally connected. This illustrates how ASCs provide adaptive benefits by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{686.000}{335.674}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{increasing access to novel information and cognitive processes.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{228.923}{428.613}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(4) Integrative (spiritual and transpersonal) mode of consciousness (IMC, for short).}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{313.354}{443.003}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the IMC, shamans explicitly sought to integrate dream processes within ritual to induce}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{327.814}{442.849}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{alterations of consciousness" (Winkelman, 2010a, p. 136). Somewhere else, you say}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{429.971}{255.845}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{emphasis). Why classify "dream states" within the}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{385.208}{429.971}{135.321}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{mode of consciousness if,}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{473.586}{442.924}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{psychedelic experience or meditation) are different from dreaming? It is not clear to me}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{488.280}{443.021}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{why the taxonomic distance between dreaming and psychedelic experience is held to}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{531.894}{442.840}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{dreaming and psychedelic experience have much more in common (Kraehenmann,}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{561.049}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{induced arousal (Fink, 1969; Sanz, Zamberlan, Erowid, Erowid, \& Tagliazucchi, 2018).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{575.742}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{And yet, if I understand it correctly, your quadripartite taxonomy of conscious modes}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{590.436}{105.412}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{suggests otherwise!}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{616.496}{443.792}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{I think that the general physiological shift from extreme autonomous nervous}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{180.115}{443.671}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{capacity) into the dream mode may be sufficient to produce the integrative mode of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{196.441}{443.648}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{consciousness, and extraordinary (but not ordinary) dream states may be one of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{213.001}{443.683}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{original platforms for selection for shamanic ASC. But clearly there are other ways}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{229.560}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{to get into the ASCs of the integrative mode of consciousness, in particular by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{245.887}{443.683}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{breaking down the coping mechanisms of the waking mode of consciousness—drugs,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{262.446}{443.674}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{sleep deprivation, extreme pain, exhaustion, fasting, long-distance running—these}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{279.006}{443.680}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{all lead to a breakdown of the waking mode and allow for new discrete states of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{295.566}{137.570}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{consciousness to emerge.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{323.554}{443.833}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{I would not necessarily insist on only 4 modes, what is lumped within the integrative}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{339.880}{443.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{mode of consciousness may ultimately be shown to involve several different modes}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{356.440}{443.773}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(i.e, sympathetic predominant versus parasympathetic predominant). I would see}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{372.999}{443.535}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{my last sentence here as my answer to your whole next question. Lead the way into}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{389.326}{443.540}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{more modes. But we have to be clear on what constitutes a mode of consciousness. I}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{405.885}{443.731}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{think a functional system is a good starting point. What can be done within a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{422.445}{231.553}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{specific set of parameters of consciousness?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{450.496}{442.873}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Before going further, it might be useful to dwell a bit longer on your definition of what}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{465.189}{65.040}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{counts as a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{145.763}{465.189}{115.448}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{mode of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{261.181}{465.189}{259.345}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{. Your model draws its inspiration from Arnold}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{479.650}{442.873}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Mandell's (1980) psychobiological model of consciousness. Mandell "suggested that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{494.344}{395.886}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{physiological mechanisms underlying "transcendent states" are based in a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{475.882}{494.344}{44.634}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{common}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{508.804}{183.308}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{underlying neurobiochemical pathway}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{261.017}{508.804}{259.514}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{" (Winkelman, 2010a, p. 25, my emphasis). Critical,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{523.498}{443.097}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{then, is the idea that different phenomenological states may be underlain by a single}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{537.959}{442.945}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{neurobiological final pathway. The problem with this definition is that it remains rather}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{552.652}{442.788}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{vague as to how modes of consciousness should be parsed. In another passage, you}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{567.113}{442.877}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{point out that "modes of consciousness are revealed in the recurrent patterns of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{581.807}{442.894}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{systemic neurophysiological functioning and their homologies with the major}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{596.267}{442.917}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{differences in experience" (Winkelman, 2010a, p. 22). So, to summarize, from what I}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{610.961}{442.959}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{understand, modes of consciousness are (i) underpinned by some basic organismic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{625.421}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{mechanisms—some basic "biological functions and organismic functions and needs"}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{640.115}{442.925}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(Winkelman, 2011, p. 29)—and, (ii) these mechanisms give rise to various altered states}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{654.576}{442.958}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{of consciousness. Importantly, modes of consciousness are more encompassing than}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{669.269}{442.835}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{states of consciousness because modes refer to the underlying neurobiological}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{683.730}{442.885}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{pathways that have the potential of generating a large range of altered states (i.e., there}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{698.424}{388.052}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{is a one-to-many mapping between each mode and its characteristic states).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{724.546}{442.686}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{We are now in a position to examine your proposal that there are exactly four modes of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{739.240}{442.930}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{consciousness. More specifically, I would like to look at the third conscious mode:}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}
\end{tikzpicture}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{64}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.286}{442.877}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{dreaming. Given what your definition of a conscious mode is, it could be argued that it}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{95.746}{442.847}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{would only make sense to distinguish between the non-dreaming deep sleep mode and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{110.440}{442.854}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the dreaming REM sleep mode if it were true that REM sleep and dreaming were}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{124.901}{442.908}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{perfectly overlapping with one another. However, as has been abundantly}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{139.594}{442.870}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{demonstrated within the last decades, a great deal of dreaming is in fact going on}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{154.055}{442.636}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{outside of REM sleep (Foulkes, 1962; Nir \& Tononi, 2010; Siclari et al., 2017; Stickgold,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{168.749}{442.861}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Malia, Fosse, Propper, \& Hobson, 2001). As a consequence, it seems that we are faced}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{183.209}{443.023}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{with a dilemma: (1) either we consider that dreaming as a whole constitutes a mode, but}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{197.903}{442.991}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{then the claim that there is a single neurobiological pathway underlying each mode will}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{212.363}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{be violated because at least two pathways—REM sleep and non-REM sleep—will be}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{227.057}{442.882}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{recognized as generating dreaming; (2) or, we split dreaming in two—REM sleep and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{241.518}{442.808}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{non-REM sleep—but then we are led to posit the existence in total of at least five modes}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{256.212}{442.863}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{of consciousness (the third one defined above being now split into two distinct modes).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{270.672}{442.745}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{In sum, either the definition of what a mode of consciousness is should be revised or}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{285.366}{443.129}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{there are actually more modes of consciousness than previously recognized. Do you}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{299.826}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{think the line of reasoning just sketched is sound? If so, which option would you be}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{314.520}{443.088}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{tempted to choose: revising the definition of modes of consciousness or recognizing the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{329.214}{251.272}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{existence of more modes than initially proposed?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{355.274}{443.602}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Certainly there are more modes to be identified, and the integrative mode of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{371.600}{443.662}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{consciousness may be too inclusive, requiring differentiation into biologically}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{388.160}{189.814}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{distinct functions of consciousness.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{416.443}{442.691}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{It seems that the remarks just made about the dreaming mode of consciousness could}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{430.904}{443.043}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{also be made about the integrative mode of consciousness. In your work, you have}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{445.598}{442.837}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{identified many key phenomenological and neurobiological differences between}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{460.292}{372.193}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{various states belonging to the integrative mode. To cite a few examples:}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{486.414}{6.380}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{83.949}{486.414}{199.994}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{Parasympathetic vs. sympathetic spiritual}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{283.932}{486.414}{236.592}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{states: "While dominant meditative traditions}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{500.874}{442.833}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{emphasize the direct approach to parasympathetic dominant states, there are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{515.568}{443.040}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{traditions that also engage the route of sympathetic stimulation, such as in the dancing}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{530.262}{382.429}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{of the Islamic mystics, the whirling dervishes." (Winkelman, 2010a, p. 131)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{556.384}{6.380}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{85.679}{556.384}{129.388}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{Meditation vs. shamanism}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{215.081}{556.384}{305.536}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{: "[Meditators'] typical activities contrast with shamans in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{570.845}{442.803}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{terms of more self-control and concentration, lower arousal, a sense of calm and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{585.538}{442.866}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{emotional detachment, a loss of sense of self, a greater awareness, and contentless}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{600.232}{212.104}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{experience." (Winkelman, 2010a, p. 132)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{626.354}{6.380}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{86.190}{626.354}{129.390}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{Shamanism vs. possession}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{215.582}{626.354}{304.939}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{: "Harner (1982) emphasized the shaman's remembering}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{640.815}{442.892}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{what happened during the soul journey as a characteristic of the shaman's SoC.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{655.509}{442.739}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Winkelman's (1986b, 1992) research supports the contention made by Eliade (1964)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{669.969}{442.928}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{that this experience is not one in which the shaman is possessed by spirits, but, rather,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{684.663}{442.792}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{one in which the shaman exercises a control over the spirits." (Winkelman, 2010a, p.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{699.123}{442.872}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{133) "A difference between shamanic flight and spirit possession is found in the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{713.817}{442.754}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{association of the latter with amnesia. Although memory does occur in some situations}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{728.278}{442.856}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{of possession, amnesia does not occur with soul flight, and in the cross-cultural data, all}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-65.268bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.233bp);

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{65}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.286}{442.808}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{cases of ASCs with amnesia are associated with possession." (Winkelman, 2010a, p.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{95.980}{29.466}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{173)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{122.102}{442.898}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{All these differences seem to support a pluralist account of the integrative mode of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{136.562}{442.747}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{consciousness. Indeed, the unity of this mode is arguably illusory and various}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{151.256}{442.875}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{"integrative" constructs should accordingly be identified. Thus, either more modes of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{165.717}{442.909}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{consciousness should be recognized, or, alternatively, the same number of conscious}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{180.410}{442.795}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{modes could be retained, but then the definition of conscious modes should be}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{195.104}{279.569}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{drastically revised. What is your view on this dilemma?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{221.164}{443.725}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{I would say that the question of the number of modes should be a question answered}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{237.490}{443.541}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{by empirical data. You have made the point about the need for a greater number of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{254.050}{443.623}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{modes. Research by Fox et al. (2016) would support the expanded mode concept,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{270.610}{443.684}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{even for meditation. Fox et al. found different patterns of brain activation and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{286.936}{443.612}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{deactivation associated with different styles of meditation (focused attention,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{303.496}{443.709}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{mantra recitation, open monitoring, and compassion/loving-kindness), as well as}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{320.055}{443.694}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{some similarities across most major meditation styles. Among their central findings}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{336.382}{443.722}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{was that the different categories of meditation had both unique psychological}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{352.941}{443.755}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{features as well as distinct patterns of activation and deactivation of different}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{369.501}{110.006}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{regions of the brain.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{397.489}{443.689}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{A similarity across different forms of meditation involves effects on mental-physical}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{414.049}{443.661}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{processes that can be progressively developed through practice, engaging an ability}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{430.608}{443.852}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{to regulate physiological and mental activities, including involuntary processes.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{446.935}{443.668}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Different meditation techniques also recruited similar areas of the brain including:}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{463.494}{443.630}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the insular cortex; the pre/supplementary motor cortices; the dorsal anterior}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{479.821}{443.700}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{cingulate cortex (involved in the regulation of attention and emotion); and the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{496.380}{443.685}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{frontopolar cortex. Fox et al. reported that the primary meditation practices (except}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{512.940}{443.680}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the loving-kindness/compassion technique) had effects on the posterior dorsolateral}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{529.500}{305.375}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{prefrontal, premotor and supplementary motor cortices.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{557.488}{443.606}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Fox et al.'s meta-analysis showed that practices of focused attention meditation}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{574.047}{443.661}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{produced significant activation both in prefrontal, premotor and dorsal anterior}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{590.374}{443.708}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{cingulate cortices, as well as slightly sub-threshold activation in the posterior}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{606.933}{443.578}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{dorsolateral prefrontal cortex and left mid insula. The focused attention meditation}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{623.493}{443.668}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{practices also resulted in a deactivation of two major default mode network hubs,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{640.053}{381.332}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the posterior cingulate cortex and the posterior inferior parietal lobule.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{668.041}{443.655}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Fox et al.'s meta-analysis of studies on open monitoring meditation techniques}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{684.600}{440.496}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{revealed significant activation in the insula, left inferior frontal gyrus, pre-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{700.927}{443.739}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{supplementary and supplementary motor area, and premotor cortex, as well as}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{717.486}{443.640}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{posterior dorsolateral region of the prefrontal cortex and the dorsal anterior}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{734.046}{94.116}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{cingulate cortex.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{66}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.223}{443.681}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{So this kind of specific brain system differences is the kind of evidence that would}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{97.550}{443.717}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{support breaking down into further modes of consciousness. But this would have to}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{114.109}{267.635}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{be on functional grounds too that I discuss below.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{142.393}{442.938}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{The reason why you call the integrative mode of consciousness integrative is that this}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{156.854}{442.954}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{mode is characterized by the integration of distinct informational units of the brain that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{171.547}{442.901}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{do not usually communicate with one another (or do so to a much lesser degree). In your}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{186.008}{442.875}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{own words, this conscious mode "produce[s] an integration of information processing}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{200.702}{442.755}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{between the R-complex [the reptilian brain] and the limbic system, between the limbic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{215.162}{442.876}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{system and the frontal cortex, and between the hemispheres of the cortex"}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{229.856}{442.845}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(Winkelman, 2011, p. 38). Overlapping with the concept of integration is the concept of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{244.317}{81.689}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{psychointegrator}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{159.319}{244.317}{361.197}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{. The latter refers to any chemical compound having the propensity to}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{259.010}{442.882}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{cause integration in the brain and in particular to "provoke limbic discharge patterns}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{273.471}{23.485}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{113.291}{273.471}{45.198}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{produce}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{170.642}{273.471}{52.561}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{enhanced}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{235.357}{273.471}{90.277}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{interhemispheric}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{337.788}{273.471}{84.806}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{synchronization}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{434.748}{273.471}{21.458}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{468.360}{273.471}{52.356}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{increased}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{288.165}{442.868}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{communicative interaction between frontal hemispheres, and between the lower brain}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{302.625}{442.867}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{areas and frontal cortex" (Winkelman, 2001, p. 220). In other words, "psychointegrator"}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{317.319}{442.866}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{is a less pejorative and more technical way to speak of "serotonergic hallucinogens"}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{331.779}{442.851}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(LSD, mescaline, psilocybin, DMT, etc.) (Winkelman, 1996, 2001, 2007). Now, what is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{346.473}{442.960}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the evidence in favor of the view that serotonergic hallucinogens have a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{361.167}{134.128}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{psychointegrative effect?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{387.289}{443.011}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Let us look first at the EEG data. One central characteristic of the integrative mode of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{401.750}{442.861}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{consciousness is that it is dominated by highly synchronized and coherent brain waves.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{416.443}{442.833}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{In particular, we would expect the EEG signal to be dominated by the high-frequency}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{430.904}{442.858}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{gamma and low-frequency theta rhythms (e.g., Winkelman, 2010a, p. 35, 2011, p. 30).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{445.598}{442.982}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Do psychointegrators effectively induce such states? The answer seems to be no. There}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{460.058}{442.832}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{is now a plethora of EEG studies available on serotonergic hallucinogens, but none of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{474.752}{443.056}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{them describe the gamma rhythm as being particularly increased by the intake of a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{489.213}{442.861}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{psychedelic compound. To my knowledge, the only exception to the rule is Eduardo}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{503.906}{442.896}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Schenberg et al.'s (2015) EEG study of ayahuasca. However, this increase in gamma}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{518.367}{442.864}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{was restricted to the second half of the experience, and importantly, it was mainly}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{533.061}{442.794}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{interpreted by the authors as being caused by harmaline (Schenberg et al., 2015, pp.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{547.521}{442.937}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{20–21), which is not a serotonergic hallucinogen (i.e., a psychointegrator) and whose}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{562.215}{442.846}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{activity probably stems chiefly from anticholinesterasic mechanisms (Yang et al., 2015;}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{576.675}{442.873}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Zhao et al., 2013; Zheng et al., 2009). As regards the increase in slow rhythms—and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{591.369}{442.861}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{theta in particular—again, to my knowledge, this electrophysiological change does not}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{605.830}{442.858}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{typically characterize psychointegrators (e.g., Muthukumaraswamy et al., 2013);}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{620.523}{442.848}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{instead, it is typical of antimuscarinic hallucinogens (Ebert, Grossmann, Oertel,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{634.984}{442.855}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Gramatté, \& Kirch, 2001; Itil, 1966; Itil \& Fink, 1966; Osipova et al., 2003), whose}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{649.678}{442.949}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{phenomenology and neurophysiology is completely different from that of serotonergic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{664.138}{442.667}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hallucinogens (Fortier, 2018a, 2019; Gyermek, 1998; Ketchum, Sidell, Crowell,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{678.832}{442.946}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Aghajanian, \& Hayes, 1973). So, looking at the EEG data, it could be objected that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{693.293}{167.391}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{typical "integrative rhythms" are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{244.955}{693.293}{16.211}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{not}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{261.172}{693.293}{259.333}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{present in psychointegrator-induced states. What}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{707.986}{140.396}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{is your take on this matter?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{67}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.223}{443.629}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{The measurement of brain waves and their various forms of coordination and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{97.550}{443.574}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{coherence is beyond my expertise. I think that nonetheless, the idea that ASC in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{114.109}{443.686}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{general, and psychedelics included, reduce the overall brain wave frequencies is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{130.669}{443.618}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{supported by diverse forms of evidence. I note you refer to "plethora of EEG studies}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{147.229}{365.101}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{available on serotonergic hallucinogens" but I did not see references.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{175.217}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Here, let me quote at length some already published material where I directly}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{191.776}{287.226}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{address these issues (Winkelman, 2017a, 2017b, 2018a):}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{219.764}{408.685}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{In spite of the diversity of entheogenic species and the broad range of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{236.324}{408.624}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{psychoactive substances, the principal psychedelics share similarities as}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{252.884}{408.687}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{tryptamines and indole alkaloids, which are sources of DMT and similar}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{269.210}{408.685}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{neurochemicals that function as agonists stimulating the serotonergic system.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{285.770}{408.630}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Serotonin has been considered the primary neurotransmitter system affected}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{302.329}{408.679}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{by psychedelics, especially through their effects at 5-HT2A receptors; action}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{318.656}{408.700}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{on other serotonin (5-HT) receptors is also established, as well as a wide range}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{335.215}{189.814}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{of other neurotransmitter systems.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{363.204}{408.584}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{The phasic effects of psychedelics first stimulate and enhance serotonin;}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{379.763}{408.793}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{secondly, saturate and overload the serotonin system; and thirdly, release the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{396.323}{408.719}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{habitual serotonin repression of the dopaminergic system. Psychedelics'}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{412.649}{408.702}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{resistance to normal reuptake mechanisms locks out serotonergic transmitter}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{429.209}{408.706}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{sites, habituating the receptors and reducing the regulatory processes of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{445.768}{408.698}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{serotonergic system. This results in a release of the dopamine system normally}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{462.095}{408.637}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{repressed by serotonin, causing a variety of visionary experiences}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{478.655}{408.779}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(hallucinations, dreams, psychosis) and modifying control and coordination}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{495.214}{408.670}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{among the major brain subsystems. Psychedelics compromise the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{511.541}{408.693}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{serotonergic inhibition of the ascending flow of information and emotional}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{528.100}{408.637}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{responses, resulting in the release of information from ancient levels of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{544.660}{408.723}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{brain that is normally inhibited by serotonin. These effects are typified by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{560.986}{408.676}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{psychedelics' interruption of cortico-striato-thalamo-cortical loops that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{577.546}{408.690}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{inhibit the lower brain structures' sensory gating systems, providing an}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{593.872}{408.783}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{enhanced availability of information managed by these brain areas}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{610.432}{269.838}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(Vollenweider, 1998; Vollenweider \& Geyer, 2001).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{638.653}{408.641}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{These psychedelic effects in altering consciousness are illustrated by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{654.980}{408.675}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Vollenweider's (1998) research on the mechanisms of action of psychedelics}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{671.539}{408.742}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{on the major cortical loops. The frontal-subcortical circuits provide one of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{688.099}{408.714}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the principal organizational networks of the brain involving neuronal}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{704.425}{408.689}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{linkages and feedback loops of the cortical areas of the frontal brain with the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{720.985}{408.676}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{thalamus of the brain stem region. Vollenweider's attributes the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{737.545}{408.653}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{consciousness-altering properties of psychedelics to their selective effects on}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

\noindent\begin{tikzpicture}[remember picture,overlay,x=1bp,y=1bp,shift={(current page.north west)}]
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-65.268bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.233bp);
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-777.332bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.466bp);
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{68}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{81.223}{408.649}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the brain's cortico-striato-thalamo-cortical feedback loops that link the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{97.550}{408.734}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{information gating systems of lower levels of the brain with the frontal}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{114.109}{405.511}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{cortex. The typical action of psychedelics interrupt the cortico-striato-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{130.669}{408.616}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{thalamo-cortical loops that inhibit the lower brain structures' sensory gating}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{146.995}{408.702}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{systems that reduce the flow of information to the frontal areas of the brain}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{163.555}{408.655}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(Vollenweider \& Geyer, 2001). Psychedelic interruption of serotonergic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{180.115}{408.701}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{inhibition of thalamic screening results in a flood of information from these}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{196.441}{408.639}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{ancient levels of the brain. This overwhelms the processing capacities of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{213.001}{408.694}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{frontal cortex and leads to alteration of experience of self, other, environment}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{229.560}{408.681}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{and produces a focus on the internal world of psychological structures and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{246.120}{65.545}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{projections.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{274.108}{408.669}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{The inhibition of dopamine release by serotonin is central to neurochemical}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{290.668}{408.679}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{balance in the brain, with the serotonergic and noradrenergic systems of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{306.994}{408.685}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{right hemisphere inhibiting the dopamine system and the left hemisphere}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{323.554}{408.699}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(Previc, 2009). This blockage of serotonin's inhibitory functions results in the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{339.880}{408.758}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{disinhibition of the dopaminergic system, releasing a flood of information}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{356.440}{408.694}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{that is normally inhibited by serotonin. The reduction of serotonergic and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{372.999}{408.628}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{noradrenergic modulation (control) results in the ascendance of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{389.326}{408.647}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{dopaminergic and acetylcholine systems that produce a variety of notable}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{405.885}{393.428}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{visual syndromes, especially hallucinations and dreaming (Hobson, 2001).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{434.107}{408.674}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Psychedelics and other alteration of consciousness share common effects on}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{450.433}{408.769}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the brain's perceptual mechanisms and representational capacities through a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{466.993}{408.702}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{temporary deregulation of the prefrontal cortex (PFC). Common effects of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{483.552}{408.682}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{this disruption are manifested in the loss of the roles of the frontal lobes and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{499.879}{408.695}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{prefrontal cortex involving higher cognitive functions. This disruption of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{516.438}{408.677}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{PFC results in the loss of various capacities—capacity for willful action,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{532.998}{408.714}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{deliberate direction of attention, and aspects of self-awareness, as well as the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{549.324}{408.709}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{capacities for abstract thought, creativity and planning. When these higher}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{565.884}{408.709}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{level brain functions of the cortical regions and the PFC are down regulated,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{582.211}{408.671}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{this allows for the manifestation of lower brain structures usually repressed}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{598.770}{408.716}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{by the PFC. This means the emergence of information and aspects of identity}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{615.330}{269.430}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{that are related to our more ancient brain regions.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{643.318}{408.689}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Psychedelic disruption of the DMN permits the operation of a more fluid and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{659.878}{408.698}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{dynamic brain lacking its usual top-down principles of control. Psychedelics}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{676.437}{408.770}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{such as LSD, psilocybin and ayahuasca cause decreases in DMN brain activity}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{692.764}{408.700}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{(Carhart-Harris et al., 2012; Carhart-Harris et al., 2014; Carhart-Harris et al.,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{709.323}{408.722}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{2016; Palhano-Fontes et al., 2015) and the disintegration of normal DMN}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{725.883}{408.685}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{functions. This is the consequence of a reduction in the connectivity of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{112.637}{742.209}{408.702}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{frontal cortex with lower brain areas (Alonso, Romero, Mañanas, \& Riba,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}
\end{tikzpicture}
