  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{80}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.286}{442.862}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{In your view, what are the key requirements that any proper naturalistic and scientific}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{95.746}{443.106}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{account of psychedelic experiences should satisfy? And what are the pitfalls that it}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{110.440}{130.843}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{should thoroughly avoid?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{136.500}{443.654}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Requirements for a mature psychedelic science must grapple with on one hand, a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{153.059}{443.673}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{recognition of a unitary basis for all kinds of knowing and believing, while on the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{169.619}{443.599}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{other hand recognizing what is the distinctive manner of knowing opened by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{185.945}{443.590}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{psychedelics. So we need a perspective that combines unity and diversity in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{202.505}{443.706}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{knowledge, and I think that means a necessary engagement with metaphysical}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{219.065}{386.693}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{dualism. What we need to avoid is ontological and metaphysical naivety.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{464.354}{219.403}{11.404}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontSymbolFallback}{13.528}{J}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{134.561}{247.238}{24.676}{ALIUSC7F7F7F}{\ALIUSFontCormorantLight}{46.647}{\ALIUSPullQuoteOpen}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{264.641}{309.259}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{Requirements for a mature psychedelic science}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{282.134}{309.201}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{must grapple with, on one hand, a recognition of a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{299.626}{309.142}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{unitary basis for all kinds of knowing and believing,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{317.119}{309.168}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{while on the other hand recognizing what is the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{334.612}{309.117}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{distinctive manner of knowing opened by}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{352.104}{309.151}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{psychedelics. […] I think that means a necessary}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{410.477}{368.986}{13.761}{ALIUSC7F7F7F}{\ALIUSFontCormorantLight}{46.647}{\ALIUSPullQuoteClose}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{158.817}{369.597}{246.912}{ALIUSC595959}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{14.694}{engagement with metaphysical dualism.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{403.849}{440.521}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{It is often assumed that hallucinogenic use is very ancient and widespread cross-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{418.309}{442.839}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{culturally. Let us call this view the "archaic hallucinogenic use hypothesis." In some}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{433.003}{442.845}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{passages, you seem to endorse this hypothesis. For example, you note that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{447.464}{442.879}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{"[p]sychedelics are associated with pre-modern religious forms and the early history of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{462.157}{308.876}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the current major world religions" (Winkelman, 2017b, p. 2).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{488.280}{442.972}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Now, it would be too long to review the ethnographic and archeological data about}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{502.973}{442.831}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hallucinogenic use through history and across cultures, but the example of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{517.434}{442.679}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Americas should suffice to illustrate why the archaic hallucinogenic use hypothesis is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{532.128}{443.112}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{arguably misleading. The New World is generally taken to be the continent where}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{546.588}{442.869}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hallucinogenic use has been the most widespread (La Barre, 1964, 1970). So, if the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{561.282}{443.018}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{archaic hallucinogenic use hypothesis is accurate, then it should at least be borne out in}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{575.742}{442.865}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the Americas; conversely, if it does not accurately depict the Amerindian data, then it is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{590.436}{150.175}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{probably wrong everywhere.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{616.559}{442.846}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{So, what is the evidence? In South America, we know that ayahuasca use (Brabec de}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{631.252}{442.898}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Mori, 2011; Gow, 1992; Shepard, 2014) and jurema use (Samorini, 2018) are relatively}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{645.713}{442.788}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{recent: probably no more than three or four centuries old. (Note that, following most}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{660.407}{442.926}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{authors, by "ayahuasca," here, I am referring to the hyperonymic category made of at}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{674.867}{26.894}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{least}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{107.472}{674.867}{98.622}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{Banisteriopsis caapi}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{206.097}{674.867}{149.117}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{plus a serotonergic plant (}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{355.219}{674.867}{85.107}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{Psychotria viridis}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{440.329}{674.867}{19.004}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{or}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{462.253}{674.867}{58.241}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{Diplopterys}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{689.561}{49.090}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{cabrerana}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{126.746}{689.561}{238.458}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{) and not to the hyponymic category made of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{366.360}{689.561}{96.754}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{Banisteriopsis caapi}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{463.157}{689.561}{57.396}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{alone: the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{704.021}{440.521}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{use of the latter is probably more ancient than the use of the former (Miller, Albarracin-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{718.715}{442.901}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Jordan, Moore, \& Capriles, 2019)). We also know that the use of anadenanthera is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{733.176}{442.999}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{ancient and was quite widespread in the Caribbean as well as in the Amazon and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

\noindent\begin{tikzpicture}[remember picture,overlay,x=1bp,y=1bp,shift={(current page.north west)}]
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-65.268bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.233bp);
  \fill[ALIUSC767171] (76.253bp,-777.332bp) rectangle ++(443.378bp,-0.466bp);
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{46.516}{344.963}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{Michael Winkelman - The evolutionary neuroanthropology of consciousness}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{505.773}{46.516}{14.471}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{81}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.286}{442.872}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Orinoco basins at the time of the arrival of the Europeans (Torres \& Repke, 2006). As}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{95.746}{442.826}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{regards the oldest use of hallucinogenic snuff, archeological data show that it was}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{110.440}{442.660}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{confined to very circumscribed places of the central Andes where rather complex}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{124.901}{442.858}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{cultures have flourished (e.g., Aschero \& Yacobaccio, 1998; Fernández Distel, 1980).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{139.594}{443.085}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{San Pedro also has a long history of use both on the Peruvian coast and in the Andes,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{154.055}{442.838}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{but there is no hard archeological data (e.g., chemical analyses) demonstrating that the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{168.749}{442.910}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{use of San Pedro is as old as that of anadenanthera (Sharon, 1972). The same goes for}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{183.209}{442.861}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{brugmansia (toé): it was used in some places in the Andes and in the lowlands, but its}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{197.903}{442.880}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{use is probably not as old as that of anadenanthera (Gayton, 1928). What about}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{212.363}{442.833}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Mesoamerica? The Spanish chroniclers and proto-ethnographers have documented}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{227.057}{442.851}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the use of several hallucinogens including various serotonergic mushrooms and peyote}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{241.518}{442.869}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(de la Garza, 1990; Heim \& Wasson, 1958, Chapter 1). However, as far as I know, there}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{256.212}{442.825}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{is no first hand description by any chronicler or proto-ethnographer of any use of these}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{270.672}{442.953}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hallucinogenic substances at the East of the Isthmus of Tehuantepec (i.e., in the Mayan}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{285.366}{442.884}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{lands) (de la Garza, 1990, Chapter 3). All that we have at the East of the Isthmus are}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{299.826}{442.731}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{somewhat far-fetched interpretations inferring hallucinogenic use from the shape of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{314.520}{203.088}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{stones (de Borhegyi, 1961); but no}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{285.481}{314.520}{22.491}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{hard}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{307.972}{314.520}{212.541}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{evidence whatsoever (Brown, 1984).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{328.981}{442.900}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Moreover, it should be noted that a culture may worship a plant or a mushroom and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{343.674}{442.863}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{produce some iconography related to this plant or mushroom without necessarily}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{358.135}{442.902}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{consuming it or consuming it but at sub-hallucinogenic doses. If we go North, there is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{372.829}{442.880}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{evidence of probably several-century-old use of datura in the Southwest (e.g.,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{387.289}{442.844}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Stevenson, 1915) but first and foremost in South and Central California (Kroeber,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{401.983}{442.873}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{1976). Nothing more in North America. Admittedly, mescal beans (Troike, 1962) and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{416.443}{442.945}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the "black drink" (Hudson, 1979) were used in the Southern Plains and in the Southeast}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{431.137}{345.461}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{of North America; however, these substances are psychoactive but}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{423.324}{431.137}{16.211}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{not}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{439.540}{431.137}{80.974}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hallucinogenic.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{445.598}{442.856}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Peyote use famously spread from the North of Mexico throughout the Great Plains up}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{460.292}{291.819}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{to Canada, but this started only at the end of the 19}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{376.423}{460.292}{144.091}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{century (La Barre, 1989).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{369.446}{460.700}{6.936}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{7.697}{th}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{474.752}{442.849}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Therefore, it is a very recent phenomenon. Wasson (1979) has argued that some}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{489.446}{442.882}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hallucinogens were used in subarctic shamanism. But the only proof he has of it is that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{503.906}{131.120}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{today some shamans use}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{209.275}{503.906}{91.015}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{Amanita muscaria}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{300.802}{503.906}{219.695}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{as a hallucinogen in their rituals. It is quite}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{518.600}{442.825}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{telling that no proto-ethnographer or explorer has ever reported the use of this}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{533.061}{427.996}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{mushroom in subarctic Amerindian cultures. It is even more telling that today}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{508.607}{533.061}{11.908}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{A.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{547.754}{44.291}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{muscaria}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{121.948}{547.754}{398.545}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{use among the Ojibwa remains restricted to few shamans and is very}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{562.215}{442.849}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{controversial (Navet, 2010). All these features betray a recent introduction and use of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{576.909}{442.864}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{the fly agaric mushroom. Finally, it must be noted that tobacco has been used in most}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{591.369}{442.849}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{regions of the Americas—including in the subarctic and circumpolar areas (Winter,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{606.063}{317.105}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{2000b, pp. 9–14)—but only in South America do we find some}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{394.723}{606.063}{69.039}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{hallucinogenic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{463.793}{606.063}{56.725}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{use of this}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{620.523}{442.880}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{plant (Wilbert, 1987). Elsewhere, it was only used at sub-hallucinogenic doses mainly}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{635.217}{442.846}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{for recreational and psychostimulant purposes (Bollwerk \& Tushingham, 2016; Winter,}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{649.911}{42.476}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{2000a).}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{676.033}{442.856}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{What can be learned from this very sketchy map of hallucinogenic use in the Americas?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{690.494}{420.471}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Well, it looks like hundreds—if not thousands—of Amerindian cultures have}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{501.957}{690.494}{16.211}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLightItalic}{12.128}{not}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{705.188}{442.869}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{traditionally used any hallucinogens. This is true of almost all cultures of North America}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{719.648}{442.876}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{(with the exception of some cultures of California and the Southwest) and of all cultures}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{734.342}{442.942}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{of the South Cone (most notably the Fuegians). It appears that many cultures of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{402.025}{783.303}{116.144}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{aliusresearch.org/bulletin}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{81.286}{442.850}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{New World did not know hallucinogens, or knew them but were not using them}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{95.746}{442.847}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hallucinogenically. This seems to be a problem for the archaic hallucinogenic use}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{110.440}{442.983}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hypothesis. By contrast, this is quite consistent with the view advocated by John}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{124.901}{442.955}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Cooper (1949) and Johannes Wilbert (1987) according to which hallucinogenic use is}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{139.594}{208.847}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{closely related to horticultural practices.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{165.717}{442.873}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Do you do endorse a full-fledged version of the "archaic hallucinogenic use hypothesis"}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{180.410}{442.923}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{or only a weaker version? How do you explain that so many cultures, even in the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{194.871}{442.806}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Americas, have apparently never used hallucinogens? Finally, regarding the etiology of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{209.565}{442.951}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{hallucinogenic use, do you side with La Barre (1970) and consider that hallucinogenic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{224.025}{442.844}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{use belongs to hunting-based cultures? Or do you alternatively side with Cooper and}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{238.719}{440.521}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{Wilbert and consider that hallucinogenic use belongs first and foremost to horticulture-}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{253.413}{81.931}{ALIUSC1F8135}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{12.128}{based cultures?}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{292.767}{443.692}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Well, there is some evidence that visionary substances—I will use this term instead}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{309.326}{443.619}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{of hallucinogen—increase in importance with horticultural societies. This may}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{325.886}{443.735}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{reflect increased knowledge, trade networks, etc. or an increased need to adjust to}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{342.212}{443.792}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{sociocultural change. But just because there is an increase in evidence for the use of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{358.772}{443.760}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{visionary plants during periods of social change does not imply that is when the use}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{375.332}{68.116}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{first started.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{403.320}{443.675}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Where visionary plants are used around the world, they are typically the purview of}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{419.879}{443.786}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{specialists and often constitute sacred and guarded knowledge. Much of tradition}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{436.206}{443.680}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{will not be passed on with cultural disintegration—or even development—as may be}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{452.766}{443.707}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{the case with the famous soma of India. Sometimes the best evidence we have of the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{469.325}{443.667}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{ancient entheogenic use of a plant are the local names which involve metaphors}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{485.885}{129.760}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{alluding to their effects.}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{513.873}{443.707}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{As to the "hard evidence" for the use of visionary substances in the past, I have}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{530.432}{443.704}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{pointed to the evidence of enhanced binding of psychedelics with the human}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{546.759}{443.758}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{serotonergic system (as opposed to other mammals). This is the hard evidence that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{563.319}{443.663}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{psychedelics influenced our evolution. Psilocybin-containing mushrooms are the}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{579.878}{443.691}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{most likely and prevalent psychedelic use in pre-history for a variety of reasons (see}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{596.205}{447.979}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{my forthcoming "Introduction" to the special issue of the Journal of Psychedelic}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{76.333}{612.764}{444.917}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{Studies on "Psychedelics in History and World Religions"). Mushrooms do not leave}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{629.324}{443.703}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{"hard" evidence unless it is placed into stone or ceramic or metal. And that is indeed}

  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{662.210}{443.707}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{America. The presence and placement of mushroom effigies and fungiform}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{678.536}{443.663}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{representations is too widespread and strategic to ignore their message. Humans}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{695.096}{443.681}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{everywhere discovered religiosity and spiritual experiences via the impulses that}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{711.656}{443.715}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{came from psilocybin-containing mushrooms. This is our human spiritual legacy, a}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{727.982}{443.650}{ALIUSC000000}{\ALIUSFontCormorantMedium}{13.528}{deep history of mushroom inspired entheogenic experiences. This impulse has risen}
  \ALIUSPlacedTextContent{77.652}{783.303}{117.883}{ALIUSC767171}{\ALIUSFontLatoLight}{10.729}{ALIUS Bulletin n°3 (2019)}
